 229: #if !MIN_VERSION_base(4,10,0)
 230: -- |Advances the given address by the given offset in bytes.
 231: --
 232: -- The new 'ForeignPtr' shares the finalizer of the original,
 233: -- equivalent from a finalization standpoint to just creating another
 234: -- reference to the original. That is, the finalizer will not be
 235: -- called before the new 'ForeignPtr' is unreachable, nor will it be
 236: -- called an additional time due to this call, and the finalizer will
 237: -- be called with the same address that it would have had this call
 238: -- not happened, *not* the new address.
 239: 
 240: {-@ measure ofForeignPtr :: GHC.ForeignPtr.ForeignPtr a -> GHC.Ptr.Ptr a @-}
 241: 
 242: 
 243: {-@ predicate FptrEnd  (ofForeignPtr P) = ((pbase (ofForeignPtr P)) + (plen (pbase (ofForeignPtr P)))) @-}
 244: {-@ predicate FPtrSize (ofForeignPtr P) = ((PtrEnd (ofForeignPtr P)) - (ofForeignPtr P)) @-}
 245: {-@ predicate FPtrValid (ofForeignPtr P) = ((pbase (ofForeignPtr P)) <= (ofForeignPtr P) && 0 < PtrSize (ofForeignPtr P)) @-}
 246: {-@ predicate FPtrValidN (ofForeignPtr P) N = ((pbase (ofForeignPtr P)) <= (ofForeignPtr P) && N < PtrSize (ofForeignPtr P)) @-}
 247: 
 248: plusForeignPtr :: ForeignPtr a -> Int -> ForeignPtr b
 249: plusForeignPtr (ForeignPtr addr guts) (I# offset) = ForeignPtr (plusAddr# addr offset) guts
 250: {-# INLINE [0] plusForeignPtr #-}
 251: {-# RULES
"ByteString plusForeignPtr/0" forall fp .
   plusForeignPtr fp 0 = fp
 #-}
 255: #endif

 276: 
 277: -- | Most operations on a 'ByteString' need to read from the buffer
 278: -- given by its @ForeignPtr Word8@ field.  But since most operations
 279: -- on @ByteString@ are (nominally) pure, their implementations cannot
 280: -- see the IO state thread that was used to initialize the contents of
 281: -- that buffer.  This means that under some circumstances, these
 282: -- buffer-reads may be executed before the writes used to initialize
 283: -- the buffer are executed, with unpredictable results.
 284: --
 285: -- 'deferForeignPtrAvailability' exists to help solve this problem.
 286: -- At runtime, a call @'deferForeignPtrAvailability' x@ is equivalent
 287: -- to @pure $! x@, but the former is more opaque to the simplifier, so
 288: -- that reads from the pointer in its result cannot be executed until
 289: -- the @'deferForeignPtrAvailability' x@ call is complete.
 290: --
 291: -- The opaque bits evaporate during CorePrep, so using
 292: -- 'deferForeignPtrAvailability' incurs no direct overhead.
 293: --
 294: -- @since 0.11.5.0
 295: deferForeignPtrAvailability :: ForeignPtr a -> IO (ForeignPtr a)
 296: forall a .

 308: unsafeDupablePerformIO :: IO a -> a
 309: -- Why does this exist? In base-4.15.1.0 until at least base-4.18.0.0,
 310: -- the version of unsafeDupablePerformIO in base prevents unboxing of
 311: -- its results with an opaque call to GHC.Exts.lazy, for reasons described
 312: -- in Note [unsafePerformIO and strictness] in GHC.IO.Unsafe. (See
 313: -- https://hackage.haskell.org/package/base-4.18.0.0/docs/src/GHC.IO.Unsafe.html#line-30 .)
 314: -- Even if we accept the (very questionable) premise that the sort of
 315: -- function described in that note should work, we expect no such
 316: -- calls to be made in the context of bytestring.  (And we really want
 317: -- unboxing!)

 322: -- -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
 323: 
 324: -- | A space-efficient representation of a 'Word8' vector, supporting many
 325: -- efficient operations.
 326: --
 327: -- A 'ByteString' contains 8-bit bytes, or by using the operations from
 328: -- "Data.ByteString.Char8" it can be interpreted as containing 8-bit
 329: -- characters.
 330: --
 331: data ByteString = BS {-# UNPACK #-} !(ForeignPtr Word8) -- payload
 332:                      {-# UNPACK #-} !Int                -- length
 333:                      -- ^ @since 0.11.0.0
 334: 
 335: -- | Type synonym for the strict flavour of 'ByteString'.
 336: --

 340: -- |
 341: -- @'PS' foreignPtr offset length@ represents a 'ByteString' with data
 342: -- backed by a given @foreignPtr@, starting at a given @offset@ in bytes
 343: -- and of a specified @length@.
 344: --
 345: -- This pattern is used to emulate the legacy 'ByteString' data
 346: -- constructor, so that pre-existing code generally doesn't need to
 347: -- change to benefit from the simplified 'BS' constructor and can
 348: -- continue to function unchanged.
 349: --
 350: -- /Note:/ Matching with this constructor will always be given a 0 offset,
 351: -- as the base will be manipulated by 'plusForeignPtr' instead.
 352: --

 477: 
 478: 
 479: -- | /O(n)/ Pack a null-terminated sequence of bytes, pointed to by an
 480: -- Addr\# (an arbitrary machine address assumed to point outside the
 481: -- garbage-collected heap) into a @ByteString@. A much faster way to
 482: -- create an 'Addr#' is with an unboxed string literal, than to pack a
 483: -- boxed string. A unboxed string literal is compiled to a static @char
 484: -- []@ by GHC. Establishing the length of the string requires a call to
 485: -- @strlen(3)@, so the 'Addr#' must point to a null-terminated buffer (as
 486: -- is the case with @\"string\"\#@ literals in GHC). Use 'Data.ByteString.Unsafe.unsafePackAddressLen'
 487: -- if you know the length of the string statically.
 488: --
 489: -- An example:
 490: --
 491: -- > literalFS = unsafePackAddress "literal"#
 492: --
 493: -- This function is /unsafe/. If you modify the buffer pointed to by the
 494: -- original 'Addr#' this modification will be reflected in the resulting
 495: -- @ByteString@, breaking referential transparency.
 496: --
 497: -- Note this also won't work if your 'Addr#' has embedded @\'\\0\'@ characters in
 498: -- the string, as @strlen@ will return too short a length.
 499: --
 500: unsafePackAddress :: Addr# -> IO ByteString
 501: lq_tmp$x##13553:GHC.Prim.Addr# -> (GHC.Types.IO Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString)unsafePackAddress GHC.Prim.Addr#addr# = do
 502: #if __GLASGOW_HASKELL__ >= 811
 503:     unsafePackLenAddress {VV##13563 : GHC.Types.Int | $k_##13564}(I# GHC.Prim.Int#(cstringLength# {lq_tmp$x##13559 : GHC.Prim.Addr# | lq_tmp$x##13559 == addr###a85p}addr#)) {lq_tmp$x##13584 : GHC.Prim.Addr# | lq_tmp$x##13584 == addr###a85p}addr#
 504: #else
 505:     l <- c_strlen (Ptr addr#)
 506:     unsafePackLenAddress (fromIntegral l) addr#
 507: #endif
 508: {-# INLINE unsafePackAddress #-}
 509: 
 510: -- | See 'unsafePackAddress'. This function is similar,
 511: -- but takes an additional length argument rather then computing
 512: -- it with @strlen@.
 513: -- Therefore embedding @\'\\0\'@ characters is possible.
 514: --
 515: -- @since 0.11.2.0
 516: unsafePackLenAddress :: Int -> Addr# -> IO ByteString

 526: -- | See 'unsafePackAddress'. This function has similar behavior. Prefer
 527: -- this function when the address in known to be an @Addr#@ literal. In
 528: -- that context, there is no need for the sequencing guarantees that 'IO'

 541: {-# INLINE unsafePackLiteral #-}
 542: 
 543: 
 544: -- | See 'unsafePackLiteral'. This function is similar,

 548: --

 580: 
 581: -- Unpacking bytestrings into lists efficiently is a tradeoff: on the one hand
 582: -- we would like to write a tight loop that just blasts the list into memory, on
 583: -- the other hand we want it to be unpacked lazily so we don't end up with a
 584: -- massive list data structure in memory.
 585: --
 586: -- Our strategy is to combine both: we will unpack lazily in reasonable sized
 587: -- chunks, where each chunk is unpacked strictly.
 588: --
 589: -- unpackBytes and unpackChars do the lazy loop, while unpackAppendBytes and
 590: -- unpackAppendChars do the chunks strictly.
 591: 
 592: unpackBytes :: ByteString -> [Word8]
 593: lq_tmp$x##21667:Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString -> [GHC.Word.Word8]unpackBytes Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteStringbs = unpackAppendBytesLazy {lq_tmp$x##21699 : Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString | lq_tmp$x##21699 == bs##a85R}bs {VV : forall a <p :: a a -> Bool>.
      {lq_tmp$x##21673 : [a]<\lq_tmp$x##21674 VV -> {lq_tmp$x##21672 : a<p lq_tmp$x##21674> | true}> | len lq_tmp$x##21673 == 0} | VV == GHC.Types.[]}[]
 594:

 872:     -- The idea here is we first do a pass over the input list to determine:
 873:     --
 874:     --  1. is a copy necessary? e.g. @concat []@, @concat [mempty, "hello"]@,
 875:     --     and @concat ["hello", mempty, mempty]@ can all be handled without
 876:     --     copying.
 877:     --  2. if a copy is necessary, how large is the result going to be?
 878:     --
 879:     -- If a copy is necessary then we create a buffer of the appropriate size
 880:     -- and do another pass over the input list, copying the chunks into the
 881:     -- buffer. Also, since foreign calls aren't entirely free we skip over
 882:     -- empty chunks while copying.
 883:     --
 884:     -- We pass the original [ByteString] (bss0) through as an argument through
 885:     -- goLen0, goLen1, and goLen since we will need it again in goCopy. Passing
 886:     -- it as an explicit argument avoids capturing it in these functions'
 887:     -- closures which would result in unnecessary closure allocation.
 888:   where
 889:     -- It's still possible that the result is empty
 890:     lq_tmp$x##20576:{VV##20563 : [{VV##20558 : Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString | $k_##20559}]<\lq_tmp$x##20578 VV -> {VV##20561 : Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString | $k_##20562[lq_tmp$x##20560:=lq_tmp$x##20578][lq_tmp$x##20574:=lq_tmp$x##20578]}> | $k_##20564} -> lq_tmp$x##20577:{VV##20570 : [{VV##20565 : Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString | $k_##20566[ds_d9cM:=lq_tmp$x##20576]}]<\lq_tmp$x##20579 VV -> {VV##20568 : Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString | $k_##20569[ds_d9cM:=lq_tmp$x##20576][lq_tmp$x##20567:=lq_tmp$x##20579][lq_tmp$x##20575:=lq_tmp$x##20579]}> | $k_##20571[ds_d9cM:=lq_tmp$x##20576]} -> {VV##20572 : Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString | $k_##20573[ds_d9cM:=lq_tmp$x##20576][ds_d9cN:=lq_tmp$x##20577]}goLen0 _    []                     = {lq_tmp$x##20605 : Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString | lq_tmp$x##20605 == Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.empty}empty

 938: 
 939: {-
Note [Float error calls out of INLINABLE things]
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~

If a function is marked INLINE or INLINABLE, then when ghc inlines or
specializes it, it duplicates the function body exactly as written.

This feature is useful for systems of rewrite rules, but sometimes
comes at a code-size cost.  One situation where this cost generally
comes with no compensating up-side is when the function in question
calls `error` or something similar.

Such an `error` call is not meaningfully improved by the extra context
inlining or specialization provides, and if inlining or specialization
happens in a different module from where the function was originally
defined, CSE will not be able to de-duplicate the error call floated
out of the inlined RHS and the error call floated out of the original
RHS.  See also https://gitlab.haskell.org/ghc/ghc/-/issues/23823

To mitigate this, we manually float the error calls out of INLINABLE
functions when it is possible to do so.
-}

                                     && lq_tmp$x##7105 ~~ lq_anf$##7205759403792830379##d9zd}"stimes"

1092: -- | This \"function\" has a superficial similarity to 'System.IO.Unsafe.unsafePerformIO' but
1093: -- it is in fact a malevolent agent of chaos. It unpicks the seams of reality
1094: -- (and the 'IO' monad) so that the normal rules no longer apply. It lulls you
1095: -- into thinking it is reasonable, but when you are not looking it stabs you
1096: -- in the back and aliases all of your mutable buffers. The carcass of many a
1097: -- seasoned Haskell programmer lie strewn at its feet.
1098: --
1099: -- Witness the trail of destruction:
1100: --
1101: -- * <https://github.com/haskell/bytestring/commit/71c4b438c675aa360c79d79acc9a491e7bbc26e7>
1102: --
1103: -- * <https://github.com/haskell/bytestring/commit/210c656390ae617d9ee3b8bcff5c88dd17cef8da>
1104: --
1105: -- * <https://github.com/haskell/aeson/commit/720b857e2e0acf2edc4f5512f2b217a89449a89d>
1106: --
1107: -- * <https://ghc.haskell.org/trac/ghc/ticket/3486>
1108: --

1112: --
1113: -- * <https://gitlab.haskell.org/ghc/ghc/-/issues/22204>
1114: --
1115: -- Do not talk about \"safe\"! You do not know what is safe!
1116: --
1117: -- Yield not to its blasphemous call! Flee traveller! Flee or you will be
1118: -- corrupted and devoured!
1119: --

1226:     :: CUInt -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1227: 
1228: foreign import ccall unsafe "static _hs_bytestring_long_long_uint_hex" c_long_long_uint_hex
1229:     :: CULLong -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1230: 
1231: foreign import ccall unsafe "static _hs_bytestring_int_dec_padded9"
1232:     c_int_dec_padded9 :: CInt -> Ptr Word8 -> IO ()
1233: 
1234: foreign import ccall unsafe "static _hs_bytestring_long_long_int_dec_padded18"
1235:     c_long_long_int_dec_padded18 :: CLLong -> Ptr Word8 -> IO ()
1236: 
1237: -- We import bytestring_is_valid_utf8 both unsafe and safe. For small inputs
1238: -- we can use the unsafe version to get a bit more performance, but for large
1239: -- inputs the safe version should be used to avoid GC synchronization pauses
1240: -- in multithreaded contexts.
1241: 
1242: foreign import ccall unsafe "bytestring_is_valid_utf8" cIsValidUtf8BA
1243:   :: ByteArray# -> CSize -> IO CInt
1244: 
1245: foreign import ccall safe "bytestring_is_valid_utf8" cIsValidUtf8BASafe
1246:   :: ByteArray# -> CSize -> IO CInt
1247: 
1248: foreign import ccall unsafe "bytestring_is_valid_utf8" cIsValidUtf8
1249:   :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO CInt
1250: 
1251: foreign import ccall safe "bytestring_is_valid_utf8" cIsValidUtf8Safe
1252:   :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO CInt
1253: 
1254: 
1255: #else
1256: 
1257: ----------------------------------------------------------------
1258: -- Haskell version of functions in fpstring.c
1259: ----------------------------------------------------------------
1260: 
1261: -- | Reverse n-bytes from the second pointer into the first
1262: c_reverse :: Ptr Word8 -> Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO ()
1263: c_reverse p1 p2 sz = Pure.reverseBytes p1 p2 (checkedCast sz)
1264: 
1265: -- | find maximum char in a packed string
1266: c_maximum :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO Word8
1267: c_maximum ptr sz = Pure.findMaximum ptr (checkedCast sz)
1268: 
1269: -- | find minimum char in a packed string
1270: c_minimum :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO Word8
1271: c_minimum ptr sz = Pure.findMinimum ptr (checkedCast sz)
1272: 
1273: -- | count the number of occurrences of a char in a string
1274: c_count :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> Word8 -> IO CSize
1275: c_count ptr sz c = checkedCast <$!> Pure.countOcc ptr (checkedCast sz) c
1276: 
1277: -- | count the number of occurrences of a char in a string
1278: c_count_ba :: ByteArray# -> Int -> Word8 -> IO CSize
1279: c_count_ba ba o c = checkedCast <$!> Pure.countOccBA ba o c
1280: 
1281: -- | duplicate a string, interspersing the character through the elements of the
1282: -- duplicated string
1283: c_intersperse :: Ptr Word8 -> Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> Word8 -> IO ()
1284: c_intersperse p1 p2 sz e = Pure.intersperse p1 p2 (checkedCast sz) e
1285: 
1286: -- | Quick sort bytes
1287: c_sort :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO ()
1288: c_sort ptr sz = Pure.quickSort ptr (checkedCast sz)
1289: 
1290: c_elem_index :: ByteArray# -> Word8 -> CSize -> IO CPtrdiff
1291: c_elem_index ba e sz = checkedCast <$!> Pure.elemIndex ba e (checkedCast sz)
1292: 
1293: cIsValidUtf8BA :: ByteArray# -> CSize -> IO CInt
1294: cIsValidUtf8BA ba sz = bool_to_cint <$> Pure.isValidUtf8BA ba (checkedCast sz)
1295: 
1296: cIsValidUtf8 :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO CInt
1297: cIsValidUtf8 ptr sz = bool_to_cint <$> Pure.isValidUtf8 ptr (checkedCast sz)
1298: 
1299: -- Pure module is compiled with `-fno-omit-yields` so it's always safe (it won't
1300: -- block on large inputs)
1301: 
1302: cIsValidUtf8BASafe :: ByteArray# -> CSize -> IO CInt
1303: cIsValidUtf8BASafe = cIsValidUtf8BA
1304: 
1305: cIsValidUtf8Safe :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO CInt
1306: cIsValidUtf8Safe = cIsValidUtf8
1307: 
1308: bool_to_cint :: Bool -> CInt
1309: bool_to_cint True = 1
1310: bool_to_cint False = 0
1311: 
1312: checkedCast :: (Bits a, Bits b, Integral a, Integral b) => a -> b
1313: checkedCast x =
1314:   fromMaybe (errorWithoutStackTrace "checkedCast: overflow")
1315:             (toIntegralSized x)
1316: 
1317: ----------------------------------------------------------------
1318: -- Haskell version of functions in itoa.c
1319: ----------------------------------------------------------------
1320: 
1321: c_int_dec :: CInt -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1322: c_int_dec = Pure.encodeSignedDec
1323: 
1324: c_long_long_int_dec :: CLLong -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1325: c_long_long_int_dec = Pure.encodeSignedDec
1326: 
1327: c_uint_dec :: CUInt -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1328: c_uint_dec = Pure.encodeUnsignedDec
1329: 
1330: c_long_long_uint_dec :: CULLong -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1331: c_long_long_uint_dec = Pure.encodeUnsignedDec
1332: 
1333: c_uint_hex :: CUInt -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1334: c_uint_hex = Pure.encodeUnsignedHex
1335: 
1336: c_long_long_uint_hex :: CULLong -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1337: c_long_long_uint_hex = Pure.encodeUnsignedHex
1338: 
1339: c_int_dec_padded9 :: CInt -> Ptr Word8 -> IO ()
1340: c_int_dec_padded9 = Pure.encodeUnsignedDecPadded 9
1341: 
1342: c_long_long_int_dec_padded18 :: CLLong -> Ptr Word8 -> IO ()
1343: c_long_long_int_dec_padded18 = Pure.encodeUnsignedDecPadded 18
1344: 
1345: #endif
